        <div class="post full-blog-post">
         <div class="post-header">
          <h2 class="post-title large">
           DIY Washi Tape Monogram Art
          </h2>
          <div class="post-meta">
           <span class="dot">
            
           </span>
           July 30, 2013
           <span class="dot">
            
           </span>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="post-tools hidden-xs hidden-sm">
          <div class="group">
           <h4 class="small-caps serif">
            Share
           </h4>
           <ul class="social-circles stacked">
            <li>
             <a class="bg-facebook social-popup" data-window-title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fliagriffith.com%2Fdiy-washi-tape-monogram-art%2F">
              <svg class="icon icon-facebook">
               <use xlink:href="#icon-facebook">
               </use>
              </svg>
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a class="bg-pinterest social-popup" data-window-title="Pinterest" href="http://pinterest.com/pin/create/link/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fliagriffith.com%2Fdiy-washi-tape-monogram-art%2F&amp;media=http%3A%2F%2Fliagriffith.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2013%2F07%2FWashiTapeMonogramsCG.jpg&amp;description=DIY+Washi+Tape+Monogram+Art">
              <svg class="icon icon-pinterest-p">
               <use xlink:href="#icon-pinterest-p">
               </use>
              </svg>
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a class="bg-twitter social-popup" data-window-title="Twitter" href="http://twitter.com/home?status=DIY+Washi+Tape+Monogram+Art+via+%40liagriffith+-+http%3A%2F%2Fliagriffith.com%2Fdiy-washi-tape-monogram-art%2F+http%3A%2F%2Fliagriffith.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2013%2F07%2FWashiTapeMonogramsCG.jpg">
              <svg class="icon icon-twitter">
               <use xlink:href="#icon-twitter">

            </li>

          <hr/>
          <div class="group">
           <h4 class="small-caps serif">
            Comment
           </h4>
           <a class="scroll" href="#comments">
            <svg class="icon icon-comment-bubbles">
             <use xlink:href="#icon-comment-bubbles">
             </use>
            </svg>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="post-body">
          <div class="post-content clearfix">
           <p>
            <a href="http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiMonogramArt.jpg">
             <span class="lg-pin-it__container">
              <span class="lg-pin-it__wrapper ">
               <img alt="Washi Tape Monogram Art" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-2591" height="648" src="http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiMonogramArt.jpg" width="560"/>
               <span class="lg-pin-it__button" data-pinterest-url="http://pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=http://liagriffith.com/diy-washi-tape-monogram-art/&amp;media=http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiMonogramArt.jpg&amp;description=DIY Washi Tape Monogram Art">
                <span class="lg-pin-it__badge">
                </span>
               </span>
              </span>
             </span>
            </a>
            My washi tape obsession continues. As you will see in tomorrows post where I tour my hallway (it is a very special hallway), I needed an update for three monogram pieces I printed a while back. They were okay, but nothing beats the playful, creative look of washi tape. I stopped by my local
            <a href="http://collagepdx.blogspot.com/" target="_blank">
             Collage
            </a>
            craft supply store and chose a selection of black and white patterned tape. Here is my simple tutorial on how to make your own framable monograms. Though I made these with black and white tape, the possibilities are endless. I can see a colorful design for a kids bedroom, something in pale patterns for a new babys room or an elegant version for the bride and groom. What a great personal gift. For my monograms I started with an Ikea
            <a href="http://www.ikea.com/us/en/catalog/products/10166368/" target="_blank">
             Ribba frame
            </a>
            with the 4.56.5 mat opening. I then printed the outline only of thick block letters would fit inside this space onto a card stock. I chose a cream card stock to be my background for the final washi covered letters in a similar color to the mat. Just follow my tutorial below to see how I formed the tape around the card stock letters, both straight and curved. You may also find pre-cut letters at a craft store that would work well for this project. Now go play with your washi tape! ~ Lia
           </p>
           <div class="inner-post-ad-container">
            <div class="inner-post-ad">
             <!-- LiaGriffith_Sidebar_1_ATF_300x250_ATF -->
             <div id="div-gpt-ad-1401071761101-1" style="width:300px; height:250px;">

             <span class="lg-pin-it__container">

               <img alt="Washi Tape Monogram" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-2592" height="677" src="http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiTapeMonogram.jpg" width="560"/>
               <span class="lg-pin-it__button" data-pinterest-url="http://pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=http://liagriffith.com/diy-washi-tape-monogram-art/&amp;media=http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiTapeMonogram.jpg&amp;description=DIY Washi Tape Monogram Art">

             <span class="lg-pin-it__container">

               <img alt="Washi Tape Monogram Tutorial" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-2593" height="1197" src="http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiTapeMonogramTutorial.jpg" width="560"/>
               <span class="lg-pin-it__button" data-pinterest-url="http://pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=http://liagriffith.com/diy-washi-tape-monogram-art/&amp;media=http://liagriffith.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/WashiTapeMonogramTutorial.jpg&amp;description=DIY Washi Tape Monogram Art">

              <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="dsq-comment-16195">
               <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-16195">
                <cite id="dsq-cite-16195">
                 <span id="dsq-author-user-16195">
                  Anthony
                 </span>
                </cite>
               </div>
               <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-16195">
                <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-16195">
                 <p>
                  Hi!!! Love love love this project! Looking for ideas on cool holiday gifts and this is so cool.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  Forgive a dumb question, but why cut the tape at an angle (when the letters are upside down)? I understand the need to leave a little to overlap but I wasnt sure about the  cutting at an angle. Also, do you find its too busy to have multiple colors on one letter? I do love your example. Hopefully a sole guy can make it right. Thanks for the inspiration!
                 </p>
                </div>
               </div>
               <ul class="children">
                <li class="comment byuser comment-author-admin bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="dsq-comment-16238">
                 <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-16238">
                  <cite id="dsq-cite-16238">
                   http://liagriffith.com
                   <span id="dsq-author-user-16238">
                    Lia
                   </span>
                  </cite>
                 </div>
                 <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-16238">
                  <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-16238">
                   <p>
                    I think you are referring to the cutting the tape at the corners of the letters, right. I do this because once you fold it in it will show again on the right side. Trimming the corners removes that excess overlap. Try it without and you will see what I mean. The nice thing about Washi is you can pull it back and do it again. I love the idea of using a lot of colors too. Maybe pick similar tones so the letter shape is apparent and less chopped? Really there is no wrong way. Share your finished pieces on my Facebook page. I would love to see them!
                   </p>
                  </div>
                 </div>
